<span id="freeTextContainer15024329488331923355"><b>5 Stars</b><br/><br/>Fantastic! 5 Stars and straight into the favourites folder! And I'll be honest and admit that I made this decision around 10 pages in - that's how much this grabbed me (and it didn't let go until the final swoon-worthy page). <br/><br/>I'm a little incoherent at the moment so I'll keep this short and say I'm ashamed it took my so long to pick up my first T.J. Klune story. I'm mostly ashamed because I knew I'd love his stories (from reading all my GR friends' fabulous reviews) and yet I still resist</span>
  <span id="freeText15024329488331923355" style="display:none"><b>5 Stars</b><br /><br />Fantastic! 5 Stars and straight into the favourites folder! And I'll be honest and admit that I made this decision around 10 pages in - that's how much this grabbed me (and it didn't let go until the final swoon-worthy page). <br /><br />I'm a little incoherent at the moment so I'll keep this short and say I'm ashamed it took my so long to pick up my first T.J. Klune story. I'm mostly ashamed because I knew I'd love his stories (from reading all my GR friends' fabulous reviews) and yet I still resisted, for stupid, crazy reasons. <br /><br />This was a fantastic M/M story about family - mainly the kind we choose for ourselves. It was an emotional read, to say the least. I laughed, I cried, I raged, I cheered, I wanted to throttle Bear on multiple occasions... and then I wanted to cuddle him close and tell him everything was going to be okay. I adored ALL of the main characters - Bear, Otter, Creed, Anna, Mrs. Paquinn, and most especially The Kid (aka Ty, the wise nine-year-old eco-terrorist in training). <br /><br />I very much loved the writing style. It was a form of storytelling that I haven't experienced much of in the past, yet I thought it worked impressively, here. <br /><br />I can't wait to read more about these fantastic characters. <br /><br /><b>Highly recommended!!! &lt;3</b></span>

<div id="review_468113907" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <span id="freeText10143967767429024862" style="display:none"><br />All roads point to Susan hating this book:<br /><br />Bad title<br />Bad cover<br />Bad 1st person POV<br />Bad female characters<br /><br />BUT, funny thing is, sometimes you just can’t predict what you’re gonna like.       <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review468113907">

<div id="review_1212361944" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1212361944" />
    <a title="Diana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15630999-diana"><img alt="Diana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1414349047p2/15630999.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1212361944?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diana" href="/user/show/15630999-diana">Diana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/15717536-bear-otter-and-the-kid">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15630999-diana?shelf=m-m">m-m</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15630999-diana?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1212361944" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3094183115820127262"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>I know I am very late to the party, but I finally read Bear, Otter and the Kid, I loved it. I had one little niggle (more on that later). <br/><br/>T.J. Klune always seems to write a story that will involve people who are family, not by blood, but by choice. The pick people that not only love unconditionally, but will have their backs at all times. That is exactly what happens in Bear, Otter and the Kid. When Bear’s mother takes off, 17 year old Bear is now responsible for raising his 6 year old </span>
  <span id="freeText3094183115820127262" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br /><br />I know I am very late to the party, but I finally read Bear, Otter and the Kid, I loved it. I had one little niggle (more on that later). <br /><br />T.J. Klune always seems to write a story that will involve people who are family, not by blood, but by choice. The pick people that not only love unconditionally, but will have their backs at all times. That is exactly what happens in Bear, Otter and the Kid. When Bear’s mother takes off, 17 year old Bear is now responsible for raising his 6 year old brother (Kid/Tyson). With the help of his friends, Anna (gf), Creed, Otter and Mrs. Paquinn, they make their own family and love and raise the Kid (Tyson).<br /> <br />There were so many sweet moments with the Kid, who just so happens to be a vegan, ecoterrorist-in-training. He is wise beyond his years, but the Kid also does a good job of taking care of his big brother, Bear. <br /><br />I absolutely adored this book, but the only niggle I had was with Bear’s inner monologue. I listened to the audiobook, so it was very confusing when he started his inner monologues. Was it happening now, or was it happening in the past? I did switch to my kindle and noticed that the monologue was in italic, which would have been easier to understand. That is the only reason I deducted .5 stars.<br /><br />Of course, I absolutely adored this book, the story and every character! I highly recommend that if you haven’t read it yet, get to it now!! I should also mentioned, the narrator, Sean Crisden, was superb. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3094183115820127262" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10356555431446597786">Oh my heart. ❤<br/><br/>Even though this is only my third book by T.J. Klune, he has quickly become an author that I will seek out. His writing is unique and witty, his stories are heartfelt and the characters he writes are amazing!<br/><br/>I loved Bear, Otter and the Kid. Creed, Anna and Mrs. Paquinn were terrific secondary characters too. My favorite though was Tyson. Known as Kid to all that loved him. ❤ He was adorably funny and oh so sweet. Wise beyond his years.   <span id="freeText10356555431446597786" style="display:none">Oh my heart. ❤<br><br>Even though this is only my third book by T.J. Klune, he has quickly become an author that I will seek out. His writing is unique and witty, his stories are heartfelt and the characters he writes are amazing!<br><br>I loved Bear, Otter and the Kid. Creed, Anna and Mrs. Paquinn were terrific secondary characters too. My favorite though was Tyson. Known as Kid to all that loved him. ❤ He was adorably funny and oh so sweet. Wise beyond his years. He had my heart from the first chapter. <br><br>At times this story wasn’t easy to read. It broke my heart. But it also brought so much happiness too. I’m not sure how the series unfolds, but for me this one seemed to be mostly Bear’s story. His journey through a storm. <br><br>Such a wonderful story about family, undefined love and unconditional friendships. <br><br>And that ending. Good thing I'm able to read on to book #2. Which by the way is up next for me. :)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1506017287i/23979583._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16279300334095735280">So, I finally did this.<br/><br/>I am guessing I should be all "OMG, I can't believe I waited so long to read this!" but honestly, I feel pretty good about having read it <i>now</i>. I might not have liked it or been able to deal with it before.   <span id="freeText16279300334095735280" style="display:none">So, I finally did this.<br /><br />I am guessing I should be all "OMG, I can't believe I waited so long to read this!" but honestly, I feel pretty good about having read it <i>now</i>. I might not have liked it or been able to deal with it before. Now, I feel glad I finally read it and I liked the Hell out of it. <br /><br />It was pretty close to true love and I think that if I read it again it probably would be. Anyway, I'll keep going and maybe come back and be totally in love. Who knows?<br /><br />What I do know is I look forward to finding out.<br /><br />Not as difficult as I thought it would be. Not easy by any means, but I was fearful and was glad I wasn't pushed too far out of my comfort zone even if some of it hurt, hurt, hurt.<br /><br />Late to the party but luckily it is a party that never ends.<br /><br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1288353927" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15005620516311217627">I am feeling that bittersweet feeling coming on as I reread one of my all-time favorite series, in preparation for the long-awaited last book. I read <i>Bear, Otter and the Kid</i>, for the first time, two years ago, and I got to discover what the fuss was all about. And I suspect (quite strongly) that I will be cursing TJ by the time this journey comes to an end. I can feel it coming.<br/><br/><br/>----------Original Review: 30 May 2015--------------<br/><b>
  <i>BR with Eleftheria and special guest, Todd!</i>
</b><br/><br/>I've heard about thi</span>
  <span id="freeText15005620516311217627" style="display:none">I am feeling that bittersweet feeling coming on as I reread one of my all-time favorite series, in preparation for the long-awaited last book. I read <i>Bear, Otter and the Kid</i>, for the first time, two years ago, and I got to discover what the fuss was all about. And I suspect (quite strongly) that I will be cursing TJ by the time this journey comes to an end. I can feel it coming.<br /><br /><br />----------Original Review: 30 May 2015--------------<br /><b>
  <i>BR with Eleftheria and special guest, Todd!</i>
</b><br /><br />I've heard about this book for ages, but didn't pick it up, until a few weeks ago, at which point I was told I <b>
  <i>must</i>
</b> read it now! And my friend Eleftheria hadn't read it, either, so we decided to do a buddy read. It was so much fun getting to talk about this book along the way.<br /><br />I'm sitting here, trying to get my thoughts together for a review and so much is bubbling up. The characters were so well written, and the narrative was engaging and funny. There was one part where I really wished the POV had switched to Otter, because it was his story, but we were hearing it from Bear. That part was a touch awkward, but other than that one piece, we're golden.<br /><br />The story is told completely from Bear's POV. When the book starts, Bear McKenna is one day shy of turning 18 and his worthless excuse for a human being, much less a parent, mother has up and left with her boyfriend of the month and left Bear to raise his five year old brother. Alone. She cleaned out his checking account before she left, but that's ok since she left him $137.50 in cash. That'll do, right? And never mind plans for college. Oh, she left a note, reminding him to pay the rent, so that should be ok. Yeah, no mother of the year award for her. You might get the impression I don't like her. Yeah, you'd be right. <br /><br />So, Bear is left with his little brother Tyson and not a clue as to how he was going to be able to take care of the Kid. And both of them end up with some serious abandonment issues because of it. He's got some awesome friends, though and they pulled together to help him through everything. His girlfriend Anna, his best friend, Creed and Creed's older brother Oliver (Otter) banded together to make sure that he know he wasn't alone in this. And his neighbor, Mrs. Paquin, too. She was brilliantly written. I want to be her when I get old (except for the being alone for 30 years part - that would suck).<br /><br />Now, Bear isn't the most introspective guy around. He's not stupid, he just doesn't think things through. He has idolized Otter, pretty much forever, but he never picked up on why. Until one night something happens between them and Bear panics and sends Otter away. And Otter stayed away for three years. And for those three years, Bear has devoted 100% of his time to Ty, not thinking about himself hardly at all. He had to grow up so fast and never got the chance to go explore the world or himself. That's kind of sad. <br /><br />But Otter returns and suddenly, Bear has to figure out why his emotions are so all over the place when Otter is around. It really took Anna and Ty to clue him in on his own feelings. Tyson is a brilliant and scary observant little guy. At nine years old, he is already way ahead of the rest of the world. And he tells it like it is. But Bear still resisted. And when he stopped resisting, he was still really wound tight over anyone knowing before he figured things out. He has a tendency to overthink things.<br /><br />It is through Bear that we get to know the other characters and I think he did a great job of it. I loved Otter and Ty. It was not difficult to see them as a family at all. They just fit. And Bear tries so hard to not let anyone down that he inevitably lets everyone down, until he remembers that he isn't alone (ok, he had to be smacked over the head with it) and lets other people help him.<br /><br />The result of it all was a story that I absolutely loved and characters I loved (Except the mom. Hated her.). I'm really looking forward to reading the rest of the series and I highly recommend what I've read, so far.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15005620516311217627" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_768941683" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/768941683" />
    <a title="* Meli Mel *" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10905711-meli-mel"><img alt="* Meli Mel *" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577750127p2/10905711.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/768941683?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="* Meli Mel *" class="user" itemprop="url" name="* Meli Mel *" href="/user/show/10905711-meli-mel">* Meli Mel *</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781613720882" href="/book/show/12360647-bear-otter-and-the-kid">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10905711-meli-mel?shelf=drama-rama-bo-bama">drama-rama-bo-bama</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10905711-meli-mel?shelf=gay-for-you">gay-for-you</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10905711-meli-mel?shelf=male-pov">male-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10905711-meli-mel?shelf=man-on-man-lovin">man-on-man-lovin</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10905711-meli-mel?shelf=uber-sweet">uber-sweet</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10905711-meli-mel?shelf=gay-sex-virgin">gay-sex-virgin</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer768941683" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8973729717056533907"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380401972i/780787._SX540_.jpg' width='125' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>♥♥♥ 5 Heart Warming/Breaking Stars ♥♥♥</b><br/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●<br/><br/>“I’ll never understand why people just won’t let others be who they are. It’s not like it’s affecting them in any way” <br/><br/>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●</b>
</blockquote><br/>This book was so wonderful. I didn't expect it to be this good. I had for a very long time but kept putting it off. I think it was the title and cover... I don't know. But I'm so glad I finally read it. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380423734i/844399._SX540_.jpg' width='405' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1387166696i/7543127._SY540_.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>======BEAR======</b><br/><br/>Bear, a.k.a Derr</span>
  <span id="freeText8973729717056533907" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380401972i/780787._SX540_.jpg" width="125" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>♥♥♥ 5 Heart Warming/Breaking Stars ♥♥♥</b><br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●<br><br>“I’ll never understand why people just won’t let others be who they are. It’s not like it’s affecting them in any way” <br><br>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●</b>
</blockquote><br>This book was so wonderful. I didn't expect it to be this good. I had for a very long time but kept putting it off. I think it was the title and cover... I don't know. But I'm so glad I finally read it. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380423734i/844399._SX540_.jpg" width="405" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1387166696i/7543127._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>======BEAR======</b><br><br>Bear, a.k.a Derrick, never in a million years thought this would happen to him. Just two day from turing eighteen, his mother has left and doesn't seem to be coming back. All she left him was $137.50 and his younger brother Ty, a.k.a. The Kid, that he is now responsible for. He was hurt, and scared. He drinks himself sick and drunk dials his best friend's older brother Otter, a.k.a. Oliver. Otter shows up to comfort him and to try to help. What ends up happening is one kiss. Bear wakes up the next day and finds Otter has left for California. He feels angry, sad, and confused about what happened between them. Three years later, Otter comes back making Bear even more confused and angry. But for some reason, he is also happy he is back.<br><br>I loved Bear! The whole book is in his POV, except for the epilogue. It was very interesting being in his head. He is a thinker, he thinks and thinks the crap out of things. He has to over analyze everything. I enjoyed his inner mononlogues. He was sarcastic and had a funny sense of humour. I loved the unconditional way he loved and cared for Ty. He had to grow up and become a father to Ty. I think he did a great job, even though he was still growing up himself. I was happy for all the support he had in his friends and even his elderly neighbour. So many times I just wanted to hug Bear, and hoped things would be better for him. I understood where he was coming from in terms of his sexuality. He has had one girlfriend, Anna, on and off since he was fourteen. Then he suddenly starts to feel things for his best friend Creed's older brother, Otter. I was frustrated with how much of a coward he was when it came to admit his feelings, but again, I got why he was that way. I still loved him, though. <br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1387166696i/7543128._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>======OTTER=====</b><br><br>Otter isn't ashamed about being gay. He has been the older brother that Bear never had. But somewhere along the way, he started to fall for Bear. And after they shared that one kiss, he felt like he was influencing him in some way that caused him to kiss him. So, he leaves to California to try to get over Bear. After three years, he knows he never will. So, he returns and hopes to have Bear any way he can in his life. Even if it's just as friends. He cares and loves both Bear and The Kid and he doesn't want to leave them again. <br><br>Oh, Otter... he made me swoon so many times. It must have been hard to be in his position, just like it was to be in Bears'. He loved Bear so much, he demonstrated it many times. He didn't want to ruin Bear's life by 'turning' him gay. But they can't deny what their hearts feel. I felt for Otter. He wanted to show everyone his love for Bear, but he couldn't because Bear was deeply buried in the closet. The chemistry between these two was wonderful to read. I couldn't get enough. Their silly banter and private jokes had me laughing. They were such a sweet and perfect couple. They really did complete each other. I loved it. And I just LOVED Otter! Seriously... he was just an amazing and supportive character.<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1387166696i/7543129._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>=====THE KID=====</b><br><br>The Kid, whose real name is Ty (a.k.a 'The vegetarian ecoterrorist-in-training'), is Bear's little brother. Ever since he learned that his mother left, following with Otter leaving as well, he has suffered with abandonment issues. He needs to constantly know where Bear is at all times. He is scared that Bear will be next to leave him. Slowly, Ty tries to move on with his life so that his brother can do the same. He is really smart, and all he wants to do is to take care of Bear. But he knows he can't do it by himself, so he relys on Otter, Creed, and Anna to help him. <br><br>Ty freaking stole my heart!! This kid is absolutely brilliant. He is only nine years old, but is the most intelligent and wise kid I have ever read about. He was absolutely endearing. The way he looks up to his brother was so heart warming. And this kid was also always there for Bear when he needed it. He would give awesome advice to Bear, which was ironic since he is just a kid, after all. But the love between Bear and Ty was beautiful. You can really feel that connection between them as you read it. I loved this kid to pieces. He was so adorable with how he would preach about how you shouldn't eat meat because of how they were killed. Instead of watching cartoons, he watches Anderson Cooper. He was quirky but very cute. Loved him!<br><br>Here's a funny and adorable quote of The Kid and Creed talking:<br><blockquote>
  <b>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●<br><br>"Veal is cow, Kid," Creed argues. "What good are cows if we can't eat them?"<br><br>"Veal is baby cows! Why would you eat baby <i>anything</i>?"<br><br>"Veal is baby cow?" Creed asks looking slightly green and horofied. "How in God's name did I not know that?"<br><br>Anna pats his arm. "I think there's a lot about a lot of things you don't know."<br><br>"It's okay, Anna," the Kid says. "I have some literature that Creed can take with him and read. It's life-changing."<br><br>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●</b>
</blockquote><br>This book was really heartbreakingly beautiful. There were many moments that hurt my heart and made me teary eyed. But there were also many romantic and funny moments that had me smiling while I read. I really enjoyed the story and LOVED the characters. I loved the writing style, which was different to what I'm use to, but I liked it nonetheless. I loved the ending, I think it was super sweet. I truly enjoyed it and I definitely recommend you give this a try. Don't let the title or the cover deter you from reading this. Just amazing.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380423734i/844399._SX540_.jpg" width="405" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="8973729717056533907" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3253212129978883778"><b>4 Stars!!</b><br/><br/>There’s not much to add to all the many reviews out there already for this book. Suffice it to say that I’m kicking myself for not reading this earlier. Honestly, I have no excuse.<br/><br/>Was this perfect? No. However, that was the beauty of it because real life isn’t perfect. Granted, Bear and the Kid have been dealt a truly harsh hand, but they’ve weathered many challenges and have persevered and even thrived. And Bear especially, handles things the best he can, despite all his neuroses.<br/><br/>What </span>
  <span id="freeText3253212129978883778" style="display:none"><b>4 Stars!!</b><br /><br />There’s not much to add to all the many reviews out there already for this book. Suffice it to say that I’m kicking myself for not reading this earlier. Honestly, I have no excuse.<br /><br />Was this perfect? No. However, that was the beauty of it because real life isn’t perfect. Granted, Bear and the Kid have been dealt a truly harsh hand, but they’ve weathered many challenges and have persevered and even thrived. And Bear especially, handles things the best he can, despite all his neuroses.<br /><br />What stands out the most here for me, is Otter. *big dreamy sigh* He was perfection. So much angst regarding the way he wanted to be what others wanted of him, that despite trying so hard there was no right or wrong way to live his life, and that he finally owned up to his feelings and executed decisions that would bring him peace and satisfaction. His love for Bear? His devotion and unwavering support? How Bear reciprocated in his own obstinate mind boggling want to slap strangle him repeatedly way? The absolute palpable intensity between these two? <br /><br /><b>The. Best. Part.</b><br /><br />You’re probably gonna cringe and possibly cry. You’ll definitely be frustrated and angry and worried. But you’ll also rejoice, laugh, and no doubt, swoon. Seriously, wholly romantic (and bonus points for being my favorite trope)!<br /></span>

<div id="review_257356047" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/257356047" />
    <a title="Sammy Goode" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5363998-sammy-goode"><img alt="Sammy Goode" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1375404347p2/5363998.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/257356047?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sammy Goode" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sammy Goode" href="/user/show/5363998-sammy-goode">Sammy Goode</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer257356047" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4274800471798330255">Never before in my life have I been at a place where I was unsure how to begin...how to tell you how I feel about a book. Never before have I had a book shake me to the very core of my being...make me laugh, cry, grit my teeth in anger, shake with relief that the end was near. Never before have I not known how to summarize a book--put it into a neat little package so that you, dear reader, could get the gist of the story, hear my thoughts and walk away to decide for yourself whether or not you w</span>
  <span id="freeText4274800471798330255" style="display:none">Never before in my life have I been at a place where I was unsure how to begin...how to tell you how I feel about a book. Never before have I had a book shake me to the very core of my being...make me laugh, cry, grit my teeth in anger, shake with relief that the end was near. Never before have I not known how to summarize a book--put it into a neat little package so that you, dear reader, could get the gist of the story, hear my thoughts and walk away to decide for yourself whether or not you would read the book. Never before have I actually ended a book, turned to page one and begun it again--right then, right away, without a moments hesitation. But this review should not be about me...no it should be about the incredible gift that T.J. Klune gave the reading world when he wrote the book, Bear, Otter, and the Kid.<br /><br />Where to begin...I have never been so in love with a family of characters in all my reading life. Bear (Derrick) is brother, father, mother, best friend, to the Kid (Tyson) after their mother, no better than a drunken whore, leaves them alone to fend for themselves. Bear's friend Creed and his on again, off again, girlfriend Anna, quickly move in to help the almost 18 year old Bear. But it is Creed's older brother Otter (Oliver) that Bear finds himself drawn to time and time again. A drunken kiss, and a fearful split sees Otter living far away for 3 years where he desperately tries to forget his love for Bear. When he returns, Bear fights him and his love tooth and nail until finally succumbing to the fact that not only is he gay but he is deeply in love with Otter. They hide their love...and too soon, Bear's mother returns to destroy that love completely...but not quite. <br /><br />I have never before apologized for a summary but this time I find myself asking for just that--forgiveness. For you see, no summary can begin to capture the magic of this story--the bliss of reading it, the incredible journey of self-discovery, love found, lost and found again and the incredibly tender relationship between these two brothers, their friends and these two men, Bear and Otter. <br /><br />I LAUGHED, I CRIED, IT MADE ME COMPLETE--truly, it did. I will end this review as I began it...never before in my reading life have I had a book that touched me to the very core of my being...you must read this book...of this I have no doubt. I do not know what else to say so I will simply say this...thank you Mr. Klune. This has been one of the loveliest experiences of my life...thank you for this gift, your book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4274800471798330255" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_196902415" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/196902415" />
    <a title="Portia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4395050-portia"><img alt="Portia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1286640997p2/4395050.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/196902415?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Portia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Portia" href="/user/show/4395050-portia">Portia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer196902415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13487894055993191327">There is no way that this is a debut novel. Somewhere there must be books under another pen name that I have yet to discover. This book is absolutely perfect. And if you knew me, you’d know that is not the opinion that should be coming out of me.<br/><br/>Why? Well, first of all, I hate books written in first person. No particular reason, just my preference. But, this book made me feel like Bear and I were sitting on his back porch and he was telling me his story. Even the flash back scenes, another liter</span>
  <span id="freeText13487894055993191327" style="display:none">There is no way that this is a debut novel. Somewhere there must be books under another pen name that I have yet to discover. This book is absolutely perfect. And if you knew me, you’d know that is not the opinion that should be coming out of me.<br /><br />Why? Well, first of all, I hate books written in first person. No particular reason, just my preference. But, this book made me feel like Bear and I were sitting on his back porch and he was telling me his story. Even the flash back scenes, another literary devise I hate, were done in such a way, that I wasn’t confused or irritated by the interruption.<br /><br />Bear is so sweet. You can almost taste his fear when he is thrust into this very adult role…the day before his 18th birthday. His girlfriend and his best friend are there to lend support, but he instinctively turns to Otter. Otter who has always been there; a steady presence in the midst of Bear’s chaotic childhood. Otter that is willing to give up a dream job in California to stay and help Bear raise the Kid.<br /><br />Jury is still out on whether Otter is a saint or a fool. Part of me wishes that he’d responded differently to Bear’s initial advances…but, that would have made for a very short book. Part of me was glad that Otter had a chance to grow up professionally and personally, so he’d be ready to be a real partner to Bear when the time was right.<br /><br />But, the real star of this book is Tyson… the Kid. The words that come out of this child’s mouth will have you rolling on the floor laughing and blushing. It’s almost a shame the Kid is straight as an arrow. Unless he does an extreme transformation during puberty, there is no way we’re getting a sequel out of him.<br /><br />This story really is about how these three souls come together to form a family. And there are plenty of obstacles. The biggest being Bear, who spends way too much time waiting for the next shoe to drop.<br /><br />I only have one question for Tj Klune…how did that woman know about San Diego?<br /><br />I would love to see this book made into a Lifetime movie. It definitely reads like a movie. Kudos to Tj Klune on a fabulous debut novel.<br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="13487894055993191327" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer307344835" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13019778645388687530">I am late to the party, everyone in the world read this before me but I will admit to liking my characters, if apart, in the same exact place mentally and emotionally, or just wishing that they were together. So Bear with his highs and lows that didn't mirror Otter's feelings, I was worried would be too much for me. Boy was I wrong. Everyone has said how much they love The Kid. I did too but my love pales beside my adoration of Bear. He's a rock and not, he's a little frayed around the edges. Bu</span>
  <span id="freeText13019778645388687530" style="display:none">I am late to the party, everyone in the world read this before me but I will admit to liking my characters, if apart, in the same exact place mentally and emotionally, or just wishing that they were together. So Bear with his highs and lows that didn't mirror Otter's feelings, I was worried would be too much for me. Boy was I wrong. Everyone has said how much they love The Kid. I did too but my love pales beside my adoration of Bear. He's a rock and not, he's a little frayed around the edges. But I was in love with all the inner monologues. His thought process is so on target for coming out and coming to grips with who he is. I loved this book; you just read and sink in. And now the sequel is right around the corner! Yeah! Can't wait.</span>

<div id="review_929647390" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/929647390" />
    <a title="Tara♥ {MindforBooks}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15615404-tara-mindforbooks"><img alt="Tara♥ {MindforBooks}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547115831p2/15615404.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/929647390?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tara♥ {MindforBooks}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tara♥ {MindforBooks}" href="/user/show/15615404-tara-mindforbooks">Tara♥ {MindforBooks}</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15615404-tara-mindforbooks?shelf=2015-books">2015-books</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15615404-tara-mindforbooks?shelf=dead-tree">dead-tree</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15615404-tara-mindforbooks?shelf=mm">mm</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15615404-tara-mindforbooks?shelf=book-crack">book-crack</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer929647390" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1989074694143635151">1st read - 11 January to 13 January (4 stars)<br/>2nd reread/listen - 21 March to 7 April 2016 (5 stars)<br/><br/>Wow!! I really loved the audio of this. So much so that I need to add another star and add to my favourites shelf for 2016. Funnily enough the things I wasn't mad on, Otter's flashback in particular, really worked in audio. <br/><br/>I really liked Sean Crisden's voice, even though it felt like he was mumbling at the end of sentences at times. I think though this might have been my headphones so I'll blame t</span>
  <span id="freeText1989074694143635151" style="display:none">1st read - 11 January to 13 January (4 stars)<br>2nd reread/listen - 21 March to 7 April 2016 (5 stars)<br><br>Wow!! I really loved the audio of this. So much so that I need to add another star and add to my favourites shelf for 2016. Funnily enough the things I wasn't mad on, Otter's flashback in particular, really worked in audio. <br><br>I really liked Sean Crisden's voice, even though it felt like he was mumbling at the end of sentences at times. I think though this might have been my headphones so I'll blame those until I get new ones. <br><br>I hated the cover of this when I read it first and now I like it. Even bought the paperback. I have no clue what that's about, some kind of brainwashing most likely!! <br><br>So onward to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13579947.Who_We_Are__Bear__Otter__and_the_Kid___2_" title="Who We Are (Bear, Otter, and the Kid, #2) by T.J. Klune" rel="nofollow noopener">Who We Are</a> which was my favourite of the two when I read them so I'm very excited. <br><br>___________________<br>Oh my, I quite liked that.<br><br>Okay so it's not perfect. Otter's flashback for example was just really very confusing but all in all I kind of fell in love with this perfectly imperfect family. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1410207726ra/11074505.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I was pretty much hooked from the start. Bear is launched into a situation which is so unfair and extremely difficult. My heart broke for him and the Kid. It wasn't just that Bear had to give up the future he had planned but the abandonment was just gut wrenching, and telling the Kid about that abandonment was so difficult to read. <br><br>I did feel myself getting mad at Bear throughout this but my mind kept going back to that letter from his mother and Otter leaving and I understood why he pushed people away and made stupid and what seemed like selfish decisions. He was always waiting for the other shoe to drop, for everyone to eventually leave him because that’s what people did. Bear was only half living and that only becomes clear when Otter comes back. <br><br>And Otter? Oh Otter. <br><br>I’m a smitten kitten. <br><br>Even though he left and he was stupid and leaving Bear and the Kid was the WORST decision he could have possibly made, and even though it took him FOREVER to stop with the self-imposed exile and come back to look after his people. I love him. I love everything about him. He is just a big cuddle bug who I want to cuddle. His heart is so good and his love for Bear and the Kid is just so beautiful. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390705919ra/8267372.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>“Bear. It’s always been you. It will always be you. I love you, and that’s why it will always be enough.”</b><br><br>The feelings of helplessness that Bear experiences throughout this book hurt my heart. He really doesn't do the right thing when the storm hits but I totally understand why he does what he does. He looks after the one person who can’t look after himself and by doing that he causes himself and the man he loves immense pain and hurt. Bear knows only that he must make sacrifices, it’s all he has known, so he lets the ocean take him. This is where the angst got real angsty people, there were tears, a lot of tears. I may have also shouted a bit.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421153279i/13330106.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But it was also where his unique family came into their own and dragged Bear to the surface. They were all pretty great but the Kid kind of stole the show. Now I’m not a fan of precocious kids in real life but in my books I love them. Ty is world wise and a bit street wise and had some disturbing information surrounding spanking and fisting that I’m not sure he needed but he was one smart kid. His insights were touching and his relationship with Bear was wonderful. <br><br><b>“I may not be the biggest Kid in the world, and I may not be the smartest, and I may not have been around to learn everything there is to know, but I do know this: people in love do the stupidest things.”</b><br><br>This story gave me the warm fuzzies. Bear and Otter are so amazing together and despite all the drama and all the mistakes that each of them made they truly do belong to each other. <br><br><b>“If someone can care about me that deeply, despite all my faults, despite all my refutations, despite all my everythings, then that makes all the storms and all the oceans worth it.”</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421153279i/13330107._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I need to know what happens next. I need to know bad.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I've read a few comments about this being very similar to the 2007 movie Shelter. I've not seen the movie so can't really comment but you may want to keep it in mind if you have seen the movie and want to read this. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="1989074694143635151" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_827915605" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/827915605" />
    <a title="Cristina T." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21090104-cristina-t"><img alt="Cristina T." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435405899p2/21090104.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/827915605?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina T." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina T." href="/user/show/21090104-cristina-t">Cristina T.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21090104-cristina-t?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21090104-cristina-t?shelf=m-m">m-m</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21090104-cristina-t?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21090104-cristina-t?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21090104-cristina-t?shelf=genre-romance">genre-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21090104-cristina-t?shelf=cr%C3%A8me-de-la-cr%C3%A8me">crème-de-la-crème</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21090104-cristina-t?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer827915605" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12441259209261232118"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433105876i/15050717._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I've had <i>Bear, Otter, and the Kid</i> on my to-read shelf for a long time, but for some reason I kept skipping it. Then I <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/554557219' rel='nofollow noopener'>read</a> that the book bore a strong resemblance to the movie <a href='http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0942384/?ref_=nv_sr_5' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shelter</a>. I <b>adore</b> that movie–it's one of my favorites–so, needless to say, I started to read the book right away. And now I want to smack myself upon the head, because I could've done myself a favor by reading this sooner. <b>I fell in love with it!!!</b> Seriously. It's utterly perfect.<br/><br/>I need to get something out of the way first</span>
  <span id="freeText12441259209261232118" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433105876i/15050717._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I've had <i>Bear, Otter, and the Kid</i> on my to-read shelf for a long time, but for some reason I kept skipping it. Then I <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/554557219" rel="nofollow noopener">read</a> that the book bore a strong resemblance to the movie <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0942384/?ref_=nv_sr_5" rel="nofollow noopener">Shelter</a>. I <b>adore</b> that movie–it's one of my favorites–so, needless to say, I started to read the book right away. And now I want to smack myself upon the head, because I could've done myself a favor by reading this sooner. <b>I fell in love with it!!!</b> Seriously. It's utterly perfect.<br><br>I need to get something out of the way first. See, I'm not a kid person, and I usually avoid books in which the MCs have kids. <b>The Kid aka Ty</b> was really awesome, though! The way he, a tiny little 9-year-old guy, took care of Bear was very endearing. And his intelligence and view on life and love kept blowing my mind...<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Then who <i>cares</i>? I'll never understand why people just won't let others be who they are. It's not like it's affecting them in any way." He turns and frowns at me. "And until you realize that," he says quietly, "how can you be fair to Otter?"</b>
</blockquote><br><br><b>Bear aka Derrick</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433107038ra/15050903.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I really felt for him, because the situation he found himself in at the age of <i>almost</i> 18 was not easy–his mom having left him and Ty on their own. It was not fair for him to have to give up his dreams at such a young age, and I could sympathize with his struggles. Mostly, I could see why he'd try to push everyone away so as to avoid being left again. Granted, I was frustrated with his choices on multiple occasions, but I couldn't really blame him.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>This is Otter, and he's home.</b>
</blockquote><br><br><b>Otter aka Oliver</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433107618ra/15051037.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Ohh, I fell hard and fast for this guy! What I loved most about him was his courage, and his willingness to fight for Bear and the Kid. He made a huge mistake when he left, but after coming back, I think he pretty much earned his place back in their lives. I admired his strength, patience and his ability to take charge and protect Bear and the Kid when needed.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>The fight for you is all I've ever known.</b>
</blockquote><br><br>Something else I really liked was the concept of <b>family</b> this book offered. I mean, we all know that we can't choose our blood relatives, but blood doesn't necessarily create bonds. And I, for one, think the people who deserve to be called family are the ones you choose for yourself. They might be relatives, they might be friends, but the important thing is for them to offer unconditional love.<br><br><b>The ending...</b> Oh, God, the ending. After all the angst and the heartbreak which ripped me apart, that ending was perfect!<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>If someone can care about me that deeply, despite all my faults, despite all my refutations, despite all my <i>everythings</i>, then that makes all the storms and all the oceans worth it.</b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433110285ra/15051378.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>* * * * *<br><br>I read this and listened to the audiobook narrated by Sean Crisden, at the same time. Mr. Crisden did a terrific job with this audio!!! <b>Loved it!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="12441259209261232118" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer199418607" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16819262418703785534">Just got through reading this one. OMG what a ride. From tears of sorrow to tears of joy, back through tears of anguish to tears of laughter. This was a remarkable book by a first time author. From start to finish I was hooked. Kid is a fantastic character, and totally believable. The things he says are awesome lol. Bear and Otter are so damn human its hard to believe they are just fictional characters.<br/><br/>The bath tub scenes were heartbreaking,but Oh the dinner on the beach scene? one of the funnie</span>
  <span id="freeText16819262418703785534" style="display:none">Just got through reading this one. OMG what a ride. From tears of sorrow to tears of joy, back through tears of anguish to tears of laughter. This was a remarkable book by a first time author. From start to finish I was hooked. Kid is a fantastic character, and totally believable. The things he says are awesome lol. Bear and Otter are so damn human its hard to believe they are just fictional characters.<br><br>The bath tub scenes were heartbreaking,but Oh the dinner on the beach scene? one of the funniest, (that has to be based on someones experiences). I laughed so hard lol. <br><br>I don't know how to put into words just how good this story was. So much happened from good to bad to worse to best. It was one continuous roller coaster, told from Bear's point of veiw but at the same time you still get to know everyone elses thoughts too. A unique way of telling the story, and a refreshing change from most of the stuff out there. <br><br>I look forward to more from this author, be it a sequal/follow on from Bear and Otter,(I so want to read more lol), to his new work thats totally along different lines.<br><br><br>OK I'm ready for book 2 now.<a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/reading%20smiley/Tipperlou_2008/Animated/smileyreadingbooks.gif?o=13" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/277741.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16819262418703785534" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ugpIx8ToV7AIZ1KtdpQjoKuR20DKF5nzH6AA7AzjgVFBNImQZ4WEqAaZDsbCwyzA+jMA05Bf4piP+cwDAsgc1g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  }

<span id="freeTextContainer5043855801576808343">TJ KLUNE is a Lambda Literary Award-winning author (Into This River I Drown) and an ex-claims examiner for an insurance company. His novels include The House in the Cerulean Sea and The Extraordinaries. Being queer himself, TJ believes it's important—now more than ever—to have accurate, positive, queer representation in stories.</span>
